{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01NN2M9GDDEut1hB5YbZVnU5","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01UByoBZejN6FBJ7TVcGvdni","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/logs/agent/sessions/plans/stateless-riding-whisper.md","content":"# Plan: Extract Shared Foreach Optimizer Step Patterns\n\n## Context\n\nThe PyTorch optimizer suite contains 11 optimizers (SGD, Adam, Adamax, Adagrad, RAdam, RMSProp, Nadam, ASGD, Rprop, AdaDelta, AdaFactor), each with a `_multi_tensor_*` function for foreach/fused parameter handling. These functions contain significant code duplication (~300-400 lines across files) with repeated patterns:\n\n- Empty parameter checks\n- Learning rate scalar conversions\n- Device/dtype grouping\n- State step increments\n- Maximize (gradient negation)\n- Weight decay handling\n- Complex parameter conversion\n- Capturable device validation\n- Sparse gradient fallbacks\n\nThis task extracts these common patterns into a shared `torch/optim/_foreach.py` module to reduce duplication while preserving algorithm-specific optimization logic in each optimizer.\n\n## Approach: Shared Module Architecture\n\n### 1. Create `torch/optim/_foreach.py`\n\nA new module exposing helper functions and utilities for multi-tensor optimization patterns.\n\n**Key Functions to Extract (shared across 9+ optimizers):**\n\n1. **`_validate_sparse_grad_empty_params()`** - Common early-exit checks\n   - Empty params check\n   - Sparse gradient assertions\n   - JIT scripting checks\n\n2. **`_prepare_lr_scalar(lr)`** - Convert tensor LR to scalar\n   - Already exists in optimizer.py as `_to_scalar()`\n   - Just import and re-export for clarity\n\n3. **`_group_params_by_device_dtype(tensor_lists, with_indices=False)`** - Group tensors by device/dtype\n   - Wrapper around `Optimizer._group_tensors_by_device_and_dtype()`\n   - Improves code readability with clearer name\n\n4. **`_increment_state_steps(state_steps)`** - Increment state steps for all params\n   - Common 6-line block (with CPU optimization comment)\n   - Appears identically in all 11 optimizers\n   - Already in adam.py lines 668-673, duplicated elsewhere\n\n5. **`_apply_maximize(device_grads)`** - Negate gradients for maximization\n   - Simple wrapper: `torch._foreach_neg(device_grads)` with type ignore\n   - Improves code clarity\n\n6. **`_apply_weight_decay(device_grads, device_params, weight_decay, maximize=False)`** - Fused weight decay\n   - Memory reuse optimization for maximize case\n   - Handles both coupled and decoupled modes\n\n7. **`_handle_complex_params(has_complex, device_params, device_grads, *state_lists)`** - Convert complex to real\n   - Wrapper around `_view_as_real()` with clearer interface\n   - Used by 10/11 optimizers\n\n8. **`_validate_capturable_devices(params, state_steps, capturable, supports_xla=False)`** - Assert capturable devices\n   - 9-line assertion block, repeated in 9 optimizers\n   - Centralizes device validation logic\n\n9. **`_handle_sparse_gradients_foreach()`** - Helper for sparse gradient fallback\n   - Used by SGD and Adagrad\n   - Determines when to fall back to single-tensor implementation\n\n**What NOT to extract (Algorithm-specific):**\n- Momentum buffer handling (SGD-specific)\n- Nesterov updates\n- EMA/exponential moving average calculations\n- Bias correction logic\n- Conditional tensor operations based on algorithm parameters\n- Beta/rho/eta coefficient calculations\n- State accumulation patterns (sum vs. mean vs. infinity norm)\n\n### 2. Update 3+ Optimizer Files\n\nModify SGD, Adam, and AdamW (+ others) to import from _foreach:\n- Remove duplicate boilerplate from `_multi_tensor_*` functions\n- Import and call shared helpers\n- Keep algorithm-specific logic intact\n- Maintain identical function signatures and behavior\n\n**Update Order (based on dependency and simplicity):**\n1. **sgd.py** - Simplest, no state steps, good reference implementation\n2. **adam.py** - Complex but widely used; uses state_steps heavily\n3. **adamw.py** - Just re-exports adam with decoupled_weight_decay=True\n4. **Others** - As time permits (adamax, adagrad, radam, rmsprop, nadam, asgd, rprop, adadelta, _adafactor)\n\n### 3. Backward Compatibility\n\n- All existing public APIs remain unchanged\n- All _multi_tensor_* functions stay with original signatures\n- Only internal organization changes\n- Existing optimizer tests should pass without modification\n- No changes needed to `__init__.py` exports\n\n## Implementation Details\n\n### File: `torch/optim/_foreach.py`\n\n```python\n# mypy: allow-untyped-defs\n\"\"\"Shared utilities for multi-tensor (foreach) optimizer implementations.\"\"\"\n\nfrom typing import cast, Optional, Union\n\nimport torch\nfrom torch import Tensor\n\nfrom .optimizer import (\n    _get_capturable_supported_devices,\n    _to_scalar,\n    _view_as_real,\n    Optimizer,\n)\n\n# Import helpers from optimizer.py to ensure single source of truth\n__all__ = [\n    \"group_params_by_device_dtype\",\n    \"increment_state_steps\",\n    \"apply_maximize\",\n    \"apply_weight_decay\",\n    \"handle_complex_params\",\n    \"validate_capturable_devices\",\n]\n\n\ndef group_params_by_device_dtype(tensor_lists, with_indices=True):\n    \"\"\"Group tensor lists by device and dtype.\"\"\"\n    return Optimizer._group_tensors_by_device_and_dtype(\n        tensor_lists, with_indices=with_indices\n    )\n\n\ndef increment_state_steps(state_steps):\n    \"\"\"Increment state steps, with CPU optimization.\"\"\"\n    # If steps are on CPU, foreach will fall back to the slow path, which is a for-loop calling t.add(1) over\n    # and over. 1 will then be wrapped into a Tensor over and over again, which is slower than if we just\n    # wrapped it once now. The alpha is required to assure we go to the right overload.\n    if not torch.compiler.is_compiling() and state_steps[0].is_cpu:\n        torch._foreach_add_(state_steps, torch.tensor(1.0, device=\"cpu\"), alpha=1.0)\n    else:\n        torch._foreach_add_(state_steps, 1)\n\n\ndef apply_maximize(device_grads):\n    \"\"\"Negate gradients for maximization mode.\"\"\"\n    if len(device_grads) == 0:\n        return device_grads\n    return torch._foreach_neg(device_grads)\n\n\ndef apply_weight_decay(device_grads, device_params, weight_decay, maximize=False):\n    \"\"\"Apply weight decay to gradients.\"\"\"\n    if weight_decay != 0:\n        # Reuse the intermediate memory (device_grads) already allocated for maximize if possible\n        if maximize:\n            torch._foreach_add_(device_grads, device_params, alpha=weight_decay)\n        else:\n            device_grads = torch._foreach_add(\n                device_grads, device_params, alpha=weight_decay\n            )\n    return device_grads\n\n\ndef handle_complex_params(has_complex, device_params, device_grads, *state_lists):\n    \"\"\"Convert complex parameters to real view for foreach ops.\"\"\"\n    if has_complex:\n        _view_as_real(device_params, device_grads, *state_lists)\n\n\ndef validate_capturable_devices(params, state_steps, capturable, supports_xla=False):\n    \"\"\"Validate that params and state_steps are on supported capturable devices.\"\"\"\n    if not torch.compiler.is_compiling() and capturable:\n        capturable_supported_devices = _get_capturable_supported_devices(\n            supports_xla=supports_xla\n        )\n        assert all(\n            p.device.type == step.device.type\n            and p.device.type in capturable_supported_devices\n            for p, step in zip(params, state_steps)\n        ), (\n            f\"If capturable=True, params and state_steps must be on supported devices: {capturable_supported_devices}.\"\n        )\n```\n\n### Updates to SGD (_multi_tensor_sgd)\n\n**Before:** 95 lines (378-471 in sgd.py)\n**After:** ~75 lines (moved empty check and grouping logic to shared module)\n\n```python\n# Key changes:\n# - Call group_params_by_device_dtype() instead of Optimizer._group_tensors_by_device_and_dtype()\n# - Call apply_maximize() instead of torch._foreach_neg()\n# - Call apply_weight_decay() instead of manual weight decay logic\n# - Early return for len(params) == 0 stays (simple, optimizer-specific check)\n```\n\n### Updates to Adam (_multi_tensor_adam)\n\n**Before:** 200+ lines\n**After:** Significant reduction with:\n- `handle_complex_params()` for complex parameter support\n- `validate_capturable_devices()` for device checks\n- `increment_state_steps()` for state step updates\n- `apply_weight_decay()` for weight decay\n- `apply_maximize()` for maximize mode\n\n### Updates to AdamW\n\n- Just re-exports Adam with `decoupled_weight_decay=True` (line 159-181)\n- No _multi_tensor_adamw exists; inherits from Adam\n- No changes needed\n\n## Files to Modify\n\n1. **Create:** `/workspace/torch/optim/_foreach.py` - New shared utilities module\n2. **Modify:** `/workspace/torch/optim/sgd.py` - Import from _foreach, simplify _multi_tensor_sgd\n3. **Modify:** `/workspace/torch/optim/adam.py` - Import from _foreach, simplify _multi_tensor_adam\n4. **Modify:** `/workspace/torch/optim/optimizer.py` (optional) - Document shared utilities\n5. **Optional:** Other 8 optimizers (adamax, adagrad, radam, rmsprop, nadam, asgd, rprop, adadelta, _adafactor)\n\n## Success Criteria\n\n✓ `/workspace/torch/optim/_foreach.py` exists with shared helper functions\n✓ SGD and Adam successfully import from and use _foreach module\n✓ All existing tests pass without modification\n✓ Code duplication reduced by ~150-200 lines across updated files\n✓ Function signatures and behavior unchanged\n✓ Backward compatibility fully maintained\n\n## Testing Strategy\n\n1. **Import validation**: Verify _foreach.py imports correctly\n2. **Existing test suite**: Run test/optim/test_optim.py (should pass unchanged)\n3. **Functional equivalence**: Compare optimizer behavior before/after refactoring\n4. **Inspect generated code**: Ensure no performance regressions in foreach ops\n\n## References\n\n- Common patterns identified in Explore agent output\n- Existing helper functions: `_to_scalar()`, `_get_value()`, `_view_as_real()`, `_get_capturable_supported_devices()`\n- Location: `/workspace/torch/optim/optimizer.py` lines 91-227\n- All _multi_tensor functions follow consistent structure documented in agent Backward Compatibility\n\n- All existing public APIs remain unchanged\n- All _multi_tensor_* functions stay with original signatures\n- Only internal organization changes\n- Existing optimizer tests should pass without modification\n- No changes needed to `__init__.py` exports\n\n## Implementation Details\n\n### File: `torch/optim/_foreach.py`\n\n```python\n# mypy: allow-untyped-defs\n\"\"\"Shared utilities for multi-tensor (foreach) optimizer implementations.\"\"\"\n\nfrom typing import cast, Optional, Union\n\nimport torch\nfrom torch import Tensor\n\nfrom .optimizer import (\n    _get_capturable_supported_devices,\n    _to_scalar,\n    _view_as_real,\n    Optimizer,\n)\n\n# Import helpers from optimizer.py to ensure single source of truth\n__all__ = [\n    \"group_params_by_device_dtype\",\n    \"increment_state_steps\",\n    \"apply_maximize\",\n    \"apply_weight_decay\",\n    \"handle_complex_params\",\n    \"validate_capturable_devices\",\n]\n\n\ndef group_params_by_device_dtype(tensor_lists, with_indices=True):\n    \"\"\"Group tensor lists by device and dtype.\"\"\"\n    return Optimizer._group_tensors_by_device_and_dtype(\n        tensor_lists, with_indices=with_indices\n    )\n\n\ndef increment_state_steps(state_steps):\n    \"\"\"Increment state steps, with CPU optimization.\"\"\"\n    # If steps are on CPU, foreach will fall back to the slow path, which is a for-loop calling t.add(1) over\n    # and over. 1 will then be wrapped into a Tensor over and over again, which is slower than if we just\n    # wrapped it once now. The alpha is required to assure we go to the right overload.\n    if not torch.compiler.is_compiling() and state_steps[0].is_cpu:\n        torch._foreach_add_(state_steps, torch.tensor(1.0, device=\"cpu\"), alpha=1.0)\n    else:\n        torch._foreach_add_(state_steps, 1)\n\n\ndef apply_maximize(device_grads):\n    \"\"\"Negate gradients for maximization mode.\"\"\"\n    if len(device_grads) == 0:\n        return device_grads\n    return torch._foreach_neg(device_grads)\n\n\ndef apply_weight_decay(device_grads, device_params, weight_decay, maximize=False):\n    \"\"\"Apply weight decay to gradients.\"\"\"\n    if weight_decay != 0:\n        # Reuse the intermediate memory (device_grads) already allocated for maximize if possible\n        if maximize:\n            torch._foreach_add_(device_grads, device_params, alpha=weight_decay)\n        else:\n            device_grads = torch._foreach_add(\n                device_grads, device_params, alpha=weight_decay\n            )\n    return device_grads\n\n\ndef handle_complex_params(has_complex, device_params, device_grads, *state_lists):\n    \"\"\"Convert complex parameters to real view for foreach ops.\"\"\"\n    if has_complex:\n        _view_as_real(device_params, device_grads, *state_lists)\n\n\ndef validate_capturable_devices(params, state_steps, capturable, supports_xla=False):\n    \"\"\"Validate that params and state_steps are on supported capturable devices.\"\"\"\n    if not torch.compiler.is_compiling() and capturable:\n        capturable_supported_devices = _get_capturable_supported_devices(\n            supports_xla=supports_xla\n        )\n        assert all(\n            p.device.type == step.device.type\n            and p.device.type in capturable_supported_devices\n            for p, step in zip(params, state_steps)\n        ), (\n            f\"If capturable=True, params and state_steps must be on supported devices: {capturable_supported_devices}.\"\n        )\n```\n\n### Updates to SGD (_multi_tensor_sgd)\n\n**Before:** 95 lines (378-471 in sgd.py)\n**After:** ~75 lines (moved empty check and grouping Common early-exit checks\n   - Empty params check\n   - Sparse gradient assertions\n   - JIT scripting checks\n\n2. **`_prepare_lr_scalar(lr)`** - Convert tensor LR to scalar\n   - Already exists in optimizer.py as `_to_scalar()`\n   - Just import and re-export for clarity\n\n3. **`_group_params_by_device_dtype(tensor_lists, with_indices=False)`** - Group tensors by device/dtype\n   - Wrapper around `Optimizer._group_tensors_by_device_and_dtype()`\n   - Improves code readability with clearer name\n\n4. **`_increment_state_steps(state_steps)`** - Increment state steps for all params\n   - Common 6-line block (with CPU optimization comment)\n   - Appears identically in all 11 optimizers\n   - Already in adam.py lines 668-673, duplicated elsewhere\n\n5. **`_apply_maximize(device_grads)`** - Negate gradients for maximization\n   - Simple wrapper: `torch._foreach_neg(device_grads)` with type ignore\n   - Improves code clarity\n\n6. **`_apply_weight_decay(device_grads, device_params, weight_decay, maximize=False)`** - Fused weight decay\n   - Memory reuse optimization for maximize case\n   - Handles both coupled and decoupled modes\n\n7. **`_handle_complex_params(has_complex, device_params, device_grads, *state_lists)`** - Convert complex to real\n   - Wrapper around `_view_as_real()` with clearer interface\n   - Used by 10/11 optimizers\n\n8. **`_validate_capturable_devices(params, state_steps, capturable, supports_xla=False)`** - Assert capturable devices\n   - 9-line assertion block, repeated in 9 optimizers\n   - Centralizes device validation logic\n\n9. **`_handle_sparse_gradients_foreach()`** - Helper for sparse gradient fallback\n   - Used by SGD and Adagrad\n   - Determines when to fall back to single-tensor implementation\n\n**What NOT to extract (Algorithm-specific):**\n- Momentum buffer handling (SGD-specific)\n- Nesterov updates\n- EMA/exponential moving average calculations\n- Bias correction logic\n- Conditional tensor operations based on algorithm parameters\n- Beta/rho/eta coefficient calculations\n- State accumulation patterns (sum vs. mean vs. infinity norm)\n\n### 2. Update 3+ Optimizer Files\n\nModify SGD, Adam, and AdamW (+ others) to import from _foreach:\n- Remove duplicate boilerplate from `_multi_tensor_*` functions\n- Import and call shared helpers\n- Keep algorithm-specific logic intact\n- Maintain identical function signatures and behavior\n\n**Update Order (based on dependency and simplicity):**\n1. **sgd.py** - Simplest, no state steps, good reference implementation\n2. **adam.py** - Complex but widely used; uses state_steps heavily\n3. **adamw.py** - Just re-exports adam with decoupled_weight_decay=True\n4. **Others** - As time permits (adamax, adagrad, radam, rmsprop, nadam, asgd, rprop, adadelta, _adafactor)\n\n### 3. Backward Compatibility\n\n- All existing public APIs remain unchanged\n- All _multi_tensor_* functions stay with original signatures\n- Only internal organization changes\n- Existing optimizer tests should pass without modification\n- No changes needed to `__init__.py` exports\n\n## Implementation Details\n\n### File: `torch/optim/_foreach.py`\n\n```python\n# mypy: allow-untyped-defs\n\"\"\"Shared utilities for multi-tensor (foreach) optimizer implementations.\"\"\"\n\nfrom typing import cast, Optional, Union\n\nimport torch\nfrom torch import Tensor\n\nfrom .optimizer import (\n    _get_capturable_supported_devices,\n    _to_scalar,\n    _view_as_real,\n    Optimizer,\n)\n\n# Import helpers from optimizer.py to ensure single source of truth\n__all__ = [\n    \"group_params_by_device_dtype\",\n    \"increment_state_steps\",\n    \"apply_maximize\",\n    \"apply_weight_decay\",\n    \"handle_complex_params\",\n    \"validate_capturable_devices\",\n]\n\n\ndef group_params_by_device_dtype(tensor_lists, with_indices=True):\n    \"\"\"Group tensor lists by device and dtype.\"\"\"\n    return Optimizer._group_tensors_by_device_and_dtype(\n        tensor_lists, with_indices=with_indices\n    )\n\n\ndef increment_state_steps(state_steps):\n    \"\"\"Increment state steps, with CPU optimization.\"\"\"\n    # If steps are on CPU, foreach will fall back to the slow path, which is a for-loop calling t.add(1) over\n    # and over. 1 will then be wrapped into a Tensor over and over again, which is slower than if we just\n    # wrapped it once now. The alpha is required to assure we go to the right overload.\n    if not torch.compiler.is_compiling() and state_steps[0].is_cpu:\n        torch._foreach_add_(state_steps, torch.tensor(1.0, device=\"cpu\"), alpha=1.0)\n    else:\n        torch._foreach_add_(state_steps, 1)\n\n\ndef apply_maximize(device_grads):\n    \"\"\"Negate gradients for maximization mode.\"\"\"\n    if len(device_grads) == 0:\n        return device_grads\n    return torch._foreach_neg(device_grads)\n\n\ndef apply_weight_decay(device_grads, device_params, weight_decay, maximize=False):\n    \"\"\"Apply weight decay to gradients.\"\"\"\n    if weight_decay != 0:\n        # Reuse the intermediate memory (device_grads) already allocated for maximize if possible\n        if maximize:\n            torch._foreach_add_(device_grads, device_params, alpha=weight_decay)\n        else:\n            device_grads = torch._foreach_add(\n                device_grads, device_params, alpha=weight_decay\n            )\n    return device_grads\n\n\ndef handle_complex_params(has_complex, device_params, device_grads, *state_lists):\n    \"\"\"Convert complex parameters to real view for foreach ops.\"\"\"\n    if has_complex:\n        _view_as_real(device_params, device_grads, *state_lists)\n\n\ndef validate_capturable_devices(params, state_steps, capturable, supports_xla=False):\n    \"\"\"Validate that params and state_steps are on supported capturable devices.\"\"\"\n    if not torch.compiler.is_compiling() and capturable:\n        capturable_supported_devices = _get_capturable_supported_devices(\n            supports_xla=supports_xla\n        )\n        assert all(\n            p.device.type == step.device.type\n            and p.device.type in capturable_supported_devices\n            for p, step in zip(params, state_steps)\n        ), (\n            f\"If capturable=True, params and state_steps must be on supported devices: {capturable_supported_devices}.\"\n        )\n```\n\n### Updates to SGD (_multi_tensor_sgd)\n\n**Before:** 95 lines (378-471 in sgd.py)\n**After:** ~75 lines (moved empty check and grouping logic to shared module)\n\n```python\n# Key changes:\n# - Call group_params_by_device_dtype() instead of Optimizer._group_tensors_by_device_and_dtype()\n# - Call apply_maximize() instead of torch._foreach_neg()\n# - Call apply_weight_decay() instead of manual weight decay logic\n# - Early return for len(params) == 0 stays (simple, optimizer-specific check)\n```\n\n### Updates to Adam (_multi_tensor_adam)\n\n**Before:** 200+ lines\n**After:** Significant reduction with:\n- `handle_complex_params()` for complex parameter support\n- `validate_capturable_devices()` for device checks\n- `increment_state_steps()` for state step updates\n- `apply_weight_decay()` for weight decay\n- `apply_maximize()` for maximize mode\n\n### Updates to AdamW\n\n- Just re-exports Adam with `decoupled_weight_decay=True` (line 159-181)\n- No _multi_tensor_adamw exists; inherits from Adam\n- No changes needed\n\n## Files to Modify\n\n1. **Create:** `/workspace/torch/optim/_foreach.py` - New shared utilities module\n2. **Modify:** `/workspace/torch/optim/sgd.py` - Import from _foreach, simplify _multi_tensor_sgd\n3. **Modify:** `/workspace/torch/optim/adam.py` - Import from _foreach, simplify _multi_tensor_adam\n4. **Modify:** `/workspace/torch/optim/optimizer.py` (optional) - Document shared utilities\n5. **Optional:** Other 8 optimizers (adamax, adagrad, radam, rmsprop, nadam, asgd, rprop, adadelta, _adafactor)\n\n## Success Criteria\n\n✓ `/workspace/torch/optim/_foreach.py` exists with shared helper functions\n✓ SGD and Adam successfully import from and use _foreach module\n✓ All existing tests pass without modification\n✓ Code duplication reduced by ~150-200 lines across updated files\n✓ Function signatures and behavior unchanged\n✓ Backward compatibility fully maintained\n\n## Testing Strategy\n\n1. **Import validation**: Verify _foreach.py imports correctly\n2. **Existing test suite**: Run test/optim/test_optim.py (should pass unchanged)\n3. **Functional equivalence**: Compare optimizer behavior before/after refactoring\n4. **Inspect generated code**: Ensure no performance regressions in foreach ops\n\n## References\n\n- Common patterns identified in Plan: Extract Shared Foreach Optimizer Step Patterns\n\n## Context\n\nThe PyTorch optimizer suite contains 11 optimizers (SGD, Adam, Adamax, Adagrad, RAdam, RMSProp, Nadam, ASGD, Rprop, AdaDelta, AdaFactor), each with a `_multi_tensor_*` function for foreach/fused parameter handling. These functions contain significant code duplication (~300-400 lines across files) with repeated patterns:\n\n- Empty parameter checks\n- Learning rate scalar conversions\n- Device/dtype grouping\n- State step increments\n- Maximize (gradient negation)\n- Weight decay handling\n- Complex parameter conversion\n- Capturable device validation\n- Sparse gradient fallbacks\n\nThis task extracts these common patterns into a shared `torch/optim/_foreach.py` module to reduce duplication while preserving algorithm-specific optimization logic in each optimizer.\n\n## Approach: Shared Module Architecture\n\n### 1. Create `torch/optim/_foreach.py`\n\nA new module exposing helper functions and utilities for multi-tensor optimization patterns.\n\n**Key Functions to Extract (shared across 9+ optimizers):**\n\n1. **`_validate_sparse_grad_empty_params()`** - Common early-exit checks\n   - Empty params check\n   - Sparse gradient assertions\n   - JIT scripting checks\n\n2. **`_prepare_lr_scalar(lr)`** - Convert tensor LR to scalar\n   - Already exists in optimizer.py as `_to_scalar()`\n   - Just import and re-export for clarity\n\n3. **`_group_params_by_device_dtype(tensor_lists, with_indices=False)`** - Group tensors by device/dtype\n   - Wrapper around `Optimizer._group_tensors_by_device_and_dtype()`\n   - Improves code readability with clearer name\n\n4. **`_increment_state_steps(state_steps)`** - Increment state steps for all params\n   - Common 6-line block (with CPU optimization comment)\n   - Appears identically in all 11 optimizers\n   - Already in adam.py lines 668-673, duplicated elsewhere\n\n5. **`_apply_maximize(device_grads)`** - Negate gradients for maximization\n   - Simple wrapper: `torch._foreach_neg(device_grads)` with type ignore\n   - Improves code clarity\n\n6. **`_apply_weight_decay(device_grads, device_params, weight_decay, maximize=False)`** - Fused weight decay\n   - Memory reuse optimization for maximize case\n   - Handles both coupled and decoupled modes\n\n7. **`_handle_complex_params(has_complex, device_params, device_grads, *state_lists)`** - Convert complex to real\n   - Wrapper around `_view_as_real()` with clearer interface\n   - Used by 10/11 optimizers\n\n8. **`_validate_capturable_devices(params, state_steps, capturable, supports_xla=False)`** - Assert capturable devices\n   - 9-line assertion block, repeated in 9 optimizers\n   - Centralizes device validation logic\n\n9. **`_handle_sparse_gradients_foreach()`** - Helper for sparse gradient fallback\n   - Used by SGD and Adagrad\n   - Determines when to fall back to single-tensor implementation\n\n**What NOT to extract (Algorithm-specific):**\n- Momentum buffer handling (SGD-specific)\n- Nesterov updates\n- EMA/exponential moving average calculations\n- Bias correction logic\n- Conditional tensor operations based on algorithm parameters\n- Beta/rho/eta coefficient calculations\n- State accumulation patterns (sum vs. mean vs. infinity norm)\n\n### 2. Update 3+ Optimizer Files\n\nModify SGD, Adam, and AdamW (+ others) to import from _foreach:\n- Remove duplicate boilerplate from `_multi_tensor_*` functions\n- Import and call shared helpers\n- Keep algorithm-specific logic intact\n- Maintain identical function signatures and behavior\n\n**Update Order (based on dependency and simplicity):**\n1. **sgd.py** - Simplest, no state steps, good reference implementation\n2. **adam.py** - Complex but widely used; uses state_steps heavily\n3. **adamw.py** - Just re-exports adam with decoupled_weight_decay=True\n4. **Others** - As time permits (adamax, adagrad, radam, rmsprop, nadam, asgd, rprop, adadelta, _adafactor)\n\n### 3. Backward Compatibility\n\n- All existing public APIs remain unchanged\n- All _multi_tensor_* functions stay with original signatures\n- Only internal organization changes\n- Existing optimizer tests should pass without modification\n- No changes needed to `__init__.py` exports\n\n## Implementation Details\n\n### File: `torch/optim/_foreach.py`\n\n```python\n# mypy: allow-untyped-defs\n\"\"\"Shared utilities for multi-tensor (foreach) optimizer implementations.\"\"\"\n\nfrom typing import cast, Optional, Union\n\nimport torch\nfrom torch import Tensor\n\nfrom .optimizer import (\n    _get_capturable_supported_devices,\n    _to_scalar,\n    _view_as_real,\n    Optimizer,\n)\n\n# Import helpers from optimizer.py to ensure single source of truth\n__all__ = [\n    \"group_params_by_device_dtype\",\n    \"increment_state_steps\",\n    \"apply_maximize\",\n    \"apply_weight_decay\",\n    \"handle_complex_params\",\n    \"validate_capturable_devices\",\n]\n\n\ndef group_params_by_device_dtype(tensor_lists, with_indices=True):\n    \"\"\"Group tensor lists by device and dtype.\"\"\"\n    return Optimizer._group_tensors_by_device_and_dtype(\n        tensor_lists, with_indices=with_indices\n    )\n\n\ndef increment_state_steps(state_steps):\n    \"\"\"Increment state steps, with CPU optimization.\"\"\"\n    # If steps are on CPU, foreach will fall back to the slow path, which is a for-loop calling t.add(1) over\n    # and over. 1 will then be wrapped into a Tensor over and over again, which is slower than if we just\n    # wrapped it once now. The alpha is required to assure we go to the right overload.\n    if not torch.compiler.is_compiling() and state_steps[0].is_cpu:\n        torch._foreach_add_(state_steps, torch.tensor(1.0, device=\"cpu\"), alpha=1.0)\n    else:\n        torch._foreach_add_(state_steps, 1)\n\n\ndef apply_maximize(device_grads):\n    \"\"\"Negate gradients for maximization mode.\"\"\"\n    if len(device_grads) == 0:\n        return device_grads\n    return torch._foreach_neg(device_grads)\n\n\ndef apply_weight_decay(device_grads, device_params, weight_decay, maximize=False):\n    \"\"\"Apply weight decay to gradients.\"\"\"\n    if weight_decay != 0:\n        # Reuse the intermediate memory (device_grads) already allocated for maximize if possible\n        if maximize:\n            torch._foreach_add_(device_grads, device_params, alpha=weight_decay)\n        else:\n            device_grads = torch._foreach_add(\n                device_grads, device_params, alpha=weight_decay\n            )\n    return device_grads\n\n\ndef handle_complex_params(has_complex, device_params, device_grads, *state_lists):\n    \"\"\"Convert complex parameters to real view for foreach ops.\"\"\"\n    if has_complex:\n        _view_as_real(device_params, device_grads, *state_lists)\n\n\ndef validate_capturable_devices(params, state_steps, capturable, supports_xla=False):\n    \"\"\"Validate that params and state_steps are on supported capturable devices.\"\"\"\n    if not torch.compiler.is_compiling() and capturable:\n        capturable_supported_devices = _get_capturable_supported_devices(\n            supports_xla=supports_xla\n        )\n        assert all(\n            p.device.type == step.device.type\n            and p.device.type in capturable_supported_devices\n            for p, step in zip(params, state_steps)\n        ), (\n            f\"If capturable=True, params and state_steps must be on supported devices: {capturable_supported_devices}.\"\n        )\n```\n\n### Updates to SGD (_multi_tensor_sgd)\n\n**Before:** 95 lines (378-471 in sgd.py)\n**After:** ~75 lines (moved empty check and grouping logic to shared module)\n\n```python\n# Key changes:\n# - Call group_params_by_device_dtype() instead of Optimizer._group_tensors_by_device_and_dtype()\n# - Call apply_maximize() instead of
